Spring and Autumn

One Crab Is Not As Good As Another 273

—Yan Qiao

These past few days, Yangcheng Lake freshwater crabs have come on the market. Perhaps influenced by Mr. Five Willows, holding a crab claw and admiring chrysanthemums is considered an elegant affair. Whether farmer, worker, merchant, student, or soldier, if they have some spare money, they must buy one to taste it, which can be counted as keeping up with the times. "Round belly in September, pointed in October," the crabs get better every day. I think that what Mr. Five Willows' descendant, Mr. Gu, felt at the seat of King Zhongyi of Wu-Yue, that "one crab is not as good as another," was just a chance encounter at the time. In reality, it must be said that one crab is better than the last. Because from the late spring and early summer, the crabs have gradually grown and improved. Once the west wind blows, they become even more substantial. The crabs in September are definitely better than those in August, and the pointed crabs in October are better than the round-bellied ones in September. It is not until next year, when the peach blossom waters rise, that the crab friends will go back to the bottom of the water to pursue the opposite sex and engage in reproduction, and then they will disappear from sight. Therefore, we only feel that eating crabs every day gets better and better.

I don't know how, but this old humorous saying, once people heard it, they borrowed it to mean "getting worse and worse," as a metaphor for human affairs. They also think that people's spiritual civilization is especially in line with this saying. When we listen to those pessimists, about everything in the modern age, except for material civilization, which one is not sighed over with "one crab is not as good as another"? Then isn't the reality of the crab and the symbolism of the crab in a relative position?

However, in the countryside, they have felt the full taste of this saying. They catch crabs very easily. In the evening, they take a lamp and a basket to the lakeside, and they can always catch a few in one evening. Because of the sharp fall in rice prices and the collapse of the rural economy in the past few years, even if they catch crabs, they are reluctant to try the new ones themselves. They have to sell them on the market to exchange them for money. Also, those who catch crabs for a living say that selling crabs now for more than 100 cash per ounce is not as profitable as selling crabs for only 10 cash per ounce more than a decade ago. Because their living expenses have increased by more than ten times. Then, the whole society has formed "one crab is not as good as another."

Briefly Discussing Various Names for Women 274

— Peng Xiang

Let's not talk about politics or romance; how about talking about women's names?

▲ Miss With the eastward movement of European customs, the title of "Miss" has almost replaced "Miss" [小姐] in terms of position. Of course, this "Miss" is only popular in "civilized" areas, such as universities and the "upper social strata." Daughters of prominent families are still called "Miss" [小姐], to show gravity. I remember last year, Shanghai newspapers reported that a certain girls' school in Peiping banned students from calling each other "Miss" and instead called them "Miss" [小姐], seemingly for the reason of preserving national culture. But in my opinion, it also feels like a lot of trouble.

▲ Vase This "vase" is also one of the newly emerging names for women. Literally, everyone can see that this is not a name with good intentions, but merely a male nickname, assigned in secret, with a hint of sarcasm. Tracing back the origin of this "vase," it should go back to a few years ago when women occupied a corner of the social professions in Shanghai. At that time, it was fashionable in offices and companies to hire a group of women; and these misses seemed to dress up a bit too much, inevitably attracting the attention of the general public in society; thus the name "vase" arose in response to the times. But the area of popularity is not wide, seemingly limited to the Shanghai area.

▲ Female Child This strange name is found in Water Margin, in Ximen Qing's words: "Godmother, come here, I ask you: Who are the young people next door, this female child [雌兒]?" Clearly, this is not a good word either, in fact containing a bit of contemptuous insult, only a great official like Ximen would dare to say it. Because people can only be divided into men and women, and not into male and female: male and female can only be applied to lower animals. Fortunately, I have not heard anyone called "female child:" probably because I live in the "middle class society." In the "lower classes" of the inland, it is still popular, but it is also unspeakable. But this can only await investigation by linguists, and will not be discussed in detail here.

Calligraphy by the famous calligrapher Xu Tiefeng

Since the calligrapher Xu Tiefeng came to Shanghai to sell his calligraphy, his career has been thriving. Xu's skill is pure and his brushwork is meticulous and intentional, without the slightest carelessness or bad habits. Because his former residence was not enough to display his work, he has now moved to a new residence at No. 5 Siming Lane, Avenue Joffre. At the same time, he has also joined with literary giants and famous calligraphers and painters from home and abroad to establish a Shangyou Literary and Art, Epigraphy, Calligraphy, and Painting Cooperative, dedicated to promoting elegance and serving society. Many people from Tianjin, Shanghai, and Peiping have joined.

▲ Widow Old Woman This is a slang term used by the "vagrants" class to call women. It occupies considerable power in the "lower class society," and it is only natural that it cannot be inserted into the "upper middle class society." But I cannot accurately know where the words "widow old woman" come from, and I have no opportunity to ask "those people." However, according to my wildest guess, this "widow old woman" seems to be similar to the transliteration of "Girl." Speaking of which, I remember that recently someone translated it as "dog girl." Although it is a transliteration, but to call women directly by "dog girl," then shouldn't men also be "male dogs"? This is exactly the same fault that the great official Ximen made.

The more I talk, the further I get, so let's "stop" here.

Remembering Shen Yichong 275

— Huang Nanding

My acquaintance with Yichong was through the introduction of my half-mad sworn brother. Initially, my fifth younger brother, Zhuan Tao, exchanged letters with Yichong, their spirits having long been acquainted. As for me, I was busily running around, only occasionally hearing his name, never once exchanging greetings. In the year of Jiazi, Qi Lu engaged in warfare, and in my old homeland of the three Wu regions, nine out of ten households moved, seeking refuge on the sea. My sworn brother, Ban Kuang, brought his family to Shanghai, and Zhuan Tao also arrived with his parents. I was staying west of Xipu, practicing the ways of a merchant, and was very happy to see them. Ban Kuang rented a place in western Shanghai. Zhuan Tao and I attended to our parents, staying in an inn. Ban Kuang would visit almost daily, gathering in one room, and many friends from the sea came to visit. Yichong was thus acquainted with me at the inn. At that time, Yichong was working in a bank. Speaking with him, he was heroic and forthright, unlike someone from the marketplace. Though Yichong dealt with petty cash daily, his nature was chivalrous. He granted all requests, enjoyed making friends, viewed gold as dirt, was a skilled drinker and speaker, and everyone who associated with him was happy. In the tenth month of winter, the disturbances of Man and Chu subsided, and my hometown was safe. Ban Kuang and Zhuan Tao agreed to return home. I was burdened with worldly affairs and did not see Yichong again. The following year, I returned to my hometown to attend to my parents, as my homeland was frequently alarmed by rumors of war. I had been separated from Yichong for two years. Zhuan Tao, however, had business on the sea and spent his days and nights with Yichong. In the sixteenth year of the Republic, Ban Kuang accepted General Bi's invitation and temporarily took charge of the secretariat, traveling with me. Passing through the sea, Yichong came to see us and hosted a banquet for Ban Kuang and me. His heroic spirit was the same as before. He drank wine like a whale sucking in hundreds of rivers, his aura vast and unparalleled. After General Bi was killed, Ban Kuang and I returned to the sea, but Yichong had suffered a business failure and was rejected by his uncle. However, his nature and spirit did not diminish as a result, and he was as philosophical as before. Later, Yichong was isolated and unable to fit in, and his circumstances became increasingly difficult. His uncle, on the other hand, was wealthy for a time but did not give him a second glance, remaining indifferent despite the pleas of friends. I, too, had no savings and could not help an old friend in need, which I still feel guilty about. During the January 28th Incident, Yichong was caught in the crossfire, and his home was destroyed. However, Yichong did not take it as a loss, only lamenting that human feelings were thinner than autumn clouds. He often seemed lost and bewildered. The other day, a friend came to tell me that Yichong had gone to the call of Xiuwen. Hearing this, Ban Kuang and I faced each other silently, not knowing that tears had wet our clothes. Recalling the past, his lofty and heroic spirit is still vivid before me. Who knew that his lifespan would not reach its end and that he would return to heaven? Alas!

▲ Short News: Yijin Grass, issued by the Peisheng Pharmaceutical Company of this city. It is said to be effective in treating pulmonary tuberculosis, hemoptysis, and other symptoms. It has been repeatedly verified by famous Chinese and Western doctors. Recently, it has also been proven by experiments conducted by Dr. Liu Guoxiang and Dr. Wang Hongyun of Shanghai Southeast Hospital. Due to insufficient space at its old address on Zhonghua Road, the company has moved this summer to Rende Lane, Zhaozhou Road, at the intersection of Dongxi Lin Road, Tangjiawan, outside the West Gate. The branch sales office in the northern city is still located in Deyu Lane, at the intersection of Yingda Road and Yinghe Road. (Star)

▲ Short News: Wujin Eye Drops were created in the Ming Dynasty by a royal physician from Lingnan. The method was traditionally passed down only to sons and daughters-in-law. It was not until the mid-Qing Dynasty that He Tongren Pharmacy was established, which has secretly manufactured this medicine for over 150 years. It is sold in South China and overseas. It is effective for all eye diseases and habitual late nights, restlessness, and insomnia. Applying it before bed has remarkable effects overnight for young people. Its side effects can also treat external hemorrhoids, boils, carbuncles, and venereal diseases. A distribution office has been established at 385A Jiujiang Road to help the world.

The Northeast Fourth Company Commander 276

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter 18: Conveying Tea With Affection, Comforting Her Husband With Sorrow; Hastily Leaving the Frontier, Forcing a Smile to Bid Farewell to Her Family

Zhao Ziqiang thought to himself, if he told his father the truth, that he would never return, his father might start crying before he even left. So, he puffed out his chest, straightened up, and shouted loudly: "Dad, I'm leaving, I'll be back this afternoon." As he spoke, his heels clicked together loudly, and he raised his hand in a military salute to his father. Suddenly, he turned around, as if on the parade ground, walking with proper steps, lifting his feet and marching out. As he walked, he looked straight ahead, not looking anywhere else, until he had walked out of Haidian Street in one breath. Only then did he turn around, stand still in a daze, looking intently at the row of rooftops on Haidian Street, while lowering his head and letting out a long sigh. Just then, he saw a cloud of dust rising at the end of the road, and the quartermaster and several brothers, driving the draft animals pulling the large cart, were running as fast as they could. The large wheels of the cart rolled on the pedestrian road, rumbling loudly. When they reached him, the quartermaster, who had been sitting on the cart, jumped down from the cart in the distance, raising his hand and saying: "Company commander, you went ahead alone." Zhao Ziqiang heard this and couldn't help but feel ashamed. He thought, "I'm really absent-minded, how could I leave them behind and go ahead alone? What did I come to Haidian for?" So he smiled and said: "I knew you would catch up, I was waiting for you here." They were smiling and talking here, and each of the servants who came with the carts held a thin whip in his hand, dragging the tips of the whips on the ground. Each person's face also had a kind of deathly gray color, especially the one in front, the carter. He wore an old blue cloth short coat with several patches on it. He was wearing a sauce-colored felt hat, the brim as soft and weak as he was, scattered down around, half covering his face. (236)

Short Story

One Morning (Part 2) 277

— Gu Mingdao

He felt that perhaps it was his wearing a suit that attracted their attention. He felt that before, when he came out, he was always with the landlord's son.

He ran back slowly. When he reached the door, he saw his cousin arguing with two children:

"Why didn't your old man come?"

"He's sick."

"Then why are you so late?"

"Sir: Can't run fast!"

"If you can't run fast, what are you doing delivering newspapers?"

"No one else to deliver them!"

From Jin Fu's mouth, he learned that these two children were the newspaper deliverer's sons and that they were being scolded because they were a little late today. Ping naturally did not agree with his cousin's actions, but he didn't dare say anything.

Another morning. Ping was waiting at the door for the newspaper deliverer. After waiting for a while, he came. A child with a newspaper bag on his back walked over from a distance. Just one child, a slightly older child. Ping grabbed his collar:

"Where's the other little kid?"

"He can't walk, he's not coming."

"Is the newspaper deliverer your dad? Was the kid who came yesterday your brother?"

"Yes."

He was silent, surprised as if he had discovered something. The newspaper delivery boy went into the house, delivered the newspaper, and came out again. He was walking back the way he came when Ping suddenly grabbed his arm

"Wait, are you going back?"

"Yes"

"I ask you: How many people are there in your family?"

"Including me, there are eight, one dad; one mom, one older sister, and four younger brothers..."

"..........................."

He stood up straight as if he were crazy: He remembered everything, he remembered that the working masses in the movie were probably them, he seemed to realize something, he also thought of his landlord uncle and cousin, he felt disgusted, felt that there were clearly two worlds丨丨two worlds of unequal wealth... He looked at the sky with a very expressive face, and raised his other hand high, and suddenly grabbed his hair. This action stunned the newspaper delivery boy:

"Sir: I have to go!" The child's voice made him realize that he was holding his arm tightly, and he smiled.

"How far is it to your house?"

"A dozen miles, less than twenty miles."

"Let's go together"

"You can't walk!"

"Nonsense! You're younger than me, why can't I walk? How do you know I can't walk?" He was secretly afraid of being discovered by his uncle's family, who would stop him.

Ping wanted to taste the bitterness of labor, and resolutely began to walk with the young newspaper vendor. He walked out of the village and onto the rice paddies, barren mounds, and wild tombs. There were only rough, narrow paths with thorns, not the wide avenues of asphalt roads. This was Ping's first attempt in his life. The fiery sun was scorching his head and back... Gradually, it became lively. Teahouses, butcher shops, lamp wick shops, and women carrying firewood on their shoulders all looked at him with unblinking eyes. Ping wanted to rest. They stepped into a small teahouse to drink tea and eat snacks. Ping saw him chewing very happily, as if he hadn't eaten breakfast. Ping thought again that he didn't have such food to eat every day. He discovered that not all children in the world have clothes to wear, food to eat, and books to read.

The two started walking forward in great strides, walking, walking, finishing their journey, reaching their destination. Although Ping was tired and his body was soaked in sweat, a happy smile appeared on his face, as if he were victorious. (The End)

Free Talk

A Glorious End 278

— Zhi Li

In these recessionary years, it seems that the ways for the petty bourgeoisie to seek stimulation have also been exhausted. One can tell by looking at the newspapers that what is taken as extraordinary news is: Jiang Minsheng shining shoes, Liang Tongfang pulling a rickshaw, "Anti-Japanese heroes ending up like this." These things have also become good topics of conversation! However, I do not understand.

I remember someone discussing Ibsen's famous play "A Doll's House," about the protagonist Nora's departure, saying: "The departure of one Nora might not be difficult, because the character is very special, the action is fresh, and she can get some people's sympathy, helping her live. Living under people's sympathy is already not free. However, if there are a hundred Noras leaving, even sympathy will be reduced. If there are a thousand or ten thousand leaving, they will be disgusted." Everyone knows that this is the truth, and there is an ancient saying to prove it: "Rarity makes things valuable."

But the circumstances of Major General Jiang Minsheng cannot be compared with Nora. First, retired generals engaging in humble occupations (?) are not considered "special" or "fresh." Second, there are certainly countless such characters, unlike Nora, who was the only one at the time. So, why do the newspaper reporters of Shanghai promote people and affairs that are not rare?

Perhaps there is a kind of indignation implied in this. Both are anti-Japanese heroes, but some are in dire straits while others are soaring to success. Is it specifically brought up for comparison? But such things are not surprising! When King Mu of Zhou conquered the south, the entire army was transformed: gentlemen became apes and cranes, and commoners became insects and sand. This has been the case since ancient times, and isn't it more prevalent today that generals make a name for themselves by exploiting the dead, and the wealthy profit from weapons? In a society where everything is unfair, what does this kind of unfairness amount to? Do the petty bourgeoisie think that all anti-Japanese heroes should be promoted and get rich?

I do not advocate "A good man should die on the battlefield" (Huang Zunxian's "Military Song"), but if a "hero" is willing to "resist Japan," then sacrificing for the country is, of course, to be expected. Fortunately, the anti-Japanese war was successful, and they escaped death. Then, retiring and seeking a profession, whether shining shoes or pulling a rickshaw, is a legitimate way to make a living, and it is indeed what a "good man" does in a bright and upright manner. What is this considered "in dire straits"? Why do they need other people's sympathy? If Jiang Minsheng and Liang Tongfang's shining shoes and pulling rickshaws are truly voluntary and not out of humble pleas or deliberately putting on a show, then the surprise of a group of petty bourgeoisie will be laughed at as "meddling in their own affairs."

Today, Jiang Minsheng and Liang Tongfang may already have people who "sympathize" with them and are helping them live, but if they willingly accept their help, they will be fooled and lose their original value. One or two Jiang Minsheng arouse interest, but more than ten Jiang Minsheng will cause people to be disgusted. The petty bourgeoisie never really have sympathy; they are just watching a play, looking for "special" and "fresh" stimulation.

Mother 279

— Liao Botan

Aunt Fushou died the day before yesterday. How did she die? Hanged herself!

Her tongue stuck out a foot long!

"A miserable person!" the villagers sighed.

She had relatives, wealthy relatives! In the city, the wealthy relatives didn't treat her badly. They gave her two dollars a month. Although she had to call them master and madam, Aunt Fushou didn't care. First, it was her fate; second, her son needed money to be raised!

She had a husband. His personality still made her doubt: the first half was as violent as a tiger, the second half as gentle as a mother to her son!

"We want to seek happiness!" In the second half, this often burst out of her husband's mouth. So, whenever there was money, the family would eat a big meal, eating until they had no money left, without considering that they would starve in the winter, starving so miserably!

In the year when the cry of soldiers not pulling laborers was loud, her husband was probably "invited" away! One "invitation" lasted ten years, and he was never seen again.

And Aunt Fushou had no choice but to go to her wealthy relatives' house to be a wet nurse!

Aunt Fushou also had sons, three or four, who all died because of poverty and disease! Fortunately, she managed to keep the last seedling for her. This year, this last seedling is sixteen years old. Marrying him a wife would complete Aunt Fushou's wish! It was also the purpose of Aunt Fushou being a wet nurse.

So, although she lost her husband, lost her sons, went through countless hardships, and still suffered afterward, she was not discouraged.

In this way, ten years passed imperceptibly in her wealthy relatives' house. She grew old! She became a little muddled in her work, and her wealthy relatives didn't like such a muddled old woman!

She came out. She packed her bags and returned to her hometown!

She didn't resent it. I can guarantee that she still wouldn't resent it even after she hanged herself. She thought: Why spend money on useless people? She even felt sorry for her previous muddleheadedness!

When she arrived in her hometown, her son could originally go to the city to sell vegetables every day to exchange for money, and she didn't need to bother anymore, but she had a wish! Her son hadn't married a wife yet.

She could weave cloth, so she opened her old, blurred eyes and wove cloth every day. Although the income from weaving cloth couldn't compare to being a wet nurse, she endured, endured, the hardship? She didn't care! The sweetness! That aftertaste.

The sweetness! That aftertaste.

Just today, the villagers carried a bamboo bed into Aunt Fushou's house.

"What?" She was imagining her son getting married, "The dowry?"

"Ah!" Aunt Fushou rolled on the ground for a long time before she came to her senses.

"Who hit him? Who hit him? ... His… breath… is… gone!"

"Bandits?"

"Ah! My son!"

………………………

Late at night, Aunt Fushou went to join him in the underworld!

Bullfighting 280

— Sheng Huanming

Alone 丨 Especially in such a quiet night, I love to meditate: Or reminisce about past events. I stared at the golden moon lying on the forest and leisurely remembered bullfighting:

In my childhood, I especially loved watching bullfighting. This is one of the rural entertainments in our hometown area. Most of the wealthier families raise fighting bulls. Once the "horn opening" period arrives, the fighting bulls from the surrounding areas all gather at a designated location. There are no special bullfighting arena buildings. The bullfighting arena is just a temporarily flooded field. Before the fight, the bull owners each hire many "helpers" to lead their bulls into the field (I remember that they were led with eight red ropes). The "helpers" are all young and strong with bare feet and thighs. In this muddy field, two bulls fight head-to-head. Each pair fights once. After winning or losing, another pair is replaced. The winner will brag and trumpet as they lead the bull back; the loser will return in despair and may even chop the bull up.

Fighting bulls are specially used for fighting and are slightly different from ordinary working bulls: their bodies are larger than ordinary bulls, and their temperament is much more fierce. They are also given names, such as Uncle Gen, whom I remember, he once raised a fighting bull named "Yuanyang." I don't know why this bull was called "Yuanyang." I only know that this is a bull that is very good at fighting and has never lost. As the "horn opening" period approached, his life became tense: busy feeding the bull, busy going to the bull pen to drive away flies, and catching blood-sucking leeches. Often, if the child who leads the bull or his own child eats a little more food, he will scold them with his eyes wide open; but he is deeply afraid that "Yuanyang" will not want to eat. He personally mixes the ingredients, and the feed, such as wheat, soybeans, and straw, is carefully selected. Especially in the one or two days before the fight, the bull eats even better: expensive things such as dates, ginseng, and "Gansheng" (1) are given to "Yuanyang" as feed. Before the fight, some people spray opium smoke on it, saying that it can increase strength. "Yuanyang" can indeed give Uncle Gen face. Every fight is a victory, even the bull of Zhao Bopi, the richest landlord in the east of the county, is defeated miserably. It is especially embarrassing for the bull of a wealthy family to be defeated. After the defeat, Zhao Bopi sticks out his small belly and says, "Damn it, what's so rare, shameless 丨 Next time we'll compete again..." He means that the people on Uncle Gen's side used conspiracy against his bull when the two bulls were fighting, making his bull "unwilling to fight." But in fact, when Zhao Bopi sold a bull named "Shuangyajiia" for the third time and came to fight "Yuanyang," it was discovered that the "demolisher" (2) had pricked "Yuanyang" on the nose with a needle. As a result, "Shuangyajiia" still ran away: The "helpers" on both sides fought into a group.

It was also on such an evening: there was a golden moon and a blue sky. During the day, Uncle Gen's "Yuanyang" had defeated the bull named Zhao Bopi's fourth bull. He returned from the city slightly drunk. At the second watch, someone discovered that he had been seriously wounded with a sharp knife under a Chinese tallow tree outside the village. He fell in a pool of blood, and could still speak lowly:

"Zhao Bopi... Give "Yuanyang" away (3)... My descendants are not allowed to raise fighting bulls丨Not allowed... Don't make a pact with Zhao 丨 Don't be able to pay taxes丨 Don't be able to... Hurry up and give Yuanyang away..."

I haven't returned to my hometown for many years, and I can't help but think of watching bullfights again. It is said that Zhao Bopi is still alive, and I don't know if Uncle Gen's children and grandchildren can still follow his instructions and not raise fighting bulls.

(1) A kind of good yellow wine. (2) Bull and bull disease, or stop fighting, or when a bull is defeated, the "demolisher" can separate the two bulls; like a referee. (3) "Give away": Sell the bull to another family.

Ruth 281

— William Wordsworth, translated by Yu Da Yin

She dwelt among the untrodden ways

Beside the springs of Dove,

A Maid whom there were none to praise

And very few to love:

A violet by a mossy stone

Half hidden from the eye!

Fair as a star, when only one

Is shining in the sky.

She lived unknown, and few could know

When Lucy ceased to be;

But she is in her grave, and, oh,

The difference to me!

Two Brothers (24) 282

— Guy de Maupassant, translated by Li Weike

When it came time to rent the place, the rent of three thousand francs stumped him because the first term of rent had to be paid upon signing, and he had nothing, he had almost nothing on him.

The small fortune his father had earned only brought in eight thousand francs a year, and he himself should not have gone so long without choosing a profession, learning this and then throwing it away, and starting to learn another, often causing his parents to be very frugal. He now had to promise to reply within two days and left the house; he suddenly had an idea to wait until Zhe'an received his inheritance and talk to him about accommodating the first term of rent for three months or even half a year.

"This is just borrowing money for a few months," he thought, "I might be able to pay him back within the year. This is a very simple matter, and he will definitely be very happy to help me with this favor."

Because it was only four o'clock and he had nothing to do, absolutely nothing to do, he went to sit in the park; he sat on the wooden bench for a long time, with no thoughts in his mind, his eyes on the ground, overcome by a kind of fatigue that came from poverty.

But the days he had spent before, from the time he came home, he spent every day like this, and he had never felt the emptiness of life and the boredom of idleness so strongly. How exactly did he spend his days from morning to night before?

He strolled along the dike at high tide, strolled on the streets, strolled in coffee shops, strolled around Marlosc, strolled everywhere. This kind of life, which had always been uneventful, now suddenly aroused his disgust and made him feel embarrassed. If he had a little money on him, he would call a car to go to the countryside and circle around those ditches covered with beech and elm trees; but he had to calculate even drinking a glass of beer and buying a cent of a stamp, so naturally there was no way to realize such an idle thought. He suddenly thought about how embarrassing it was for a person over thirty to have to constantly ask his mother for a louis (equivalent to twenty francs) with a red face; he scratched the ground with his cane and mumbled:

"Ah! If I had money!"

Then the thought of his brother getting the inheritance flashed through his mind like being stung by a bee; but he didn't want to fall into jealousy, and he anxiously drove the thought away.

Some children were playing in the dust on the road beside him. These were all children with long golden hair, and they seemed very serious and very careful, piling sand into small mountains, and then stomping on them with one foot.

Bill's mood was very melancholy that day. On such days, we will think of all kinds of thoughts and search for all the inner feelings.

"Our labor is the same as the work of these little tricks," he thought. Then he thought that perhaps the wisest way to live was to raise two or three such useless little things and then watch them grow up with satisfaction and curiosity. The idea of getting married gently brushed in front of him. Married, no longer alone, he would not be so lonely. When our hearts are shaking, at least we can hear someone moving beside us, and when we are in pain, being able to say "you" to a woman is already not so lonely.

He began to think about women.

He really knew very few women, because he only had some half-month unions in the Latin Quarter, which would break up when the money ran out this month, and then they would reunite or find another one when there was money next month. But he thought that there were always some very pure, very docile, and very comforting women in the world. Was his home not orderly and extremely lovely because of his mother? How he yearned to know a woman, a real woman!

He suddenly stood up and decided to go see Mrs. Luezime.

Talking

"Stalemate" 283

— Wei Ba

As I have never studied tactics, I do not know how many types there are. However, from my experience reading newspapers, I know that in terms of terrain, there are distinctions between field battles, street battles, air battles, and naval battles; in terms of weapons, there are infantry battles, artillery battles, and methods such as broadsword fighting and hand-to-hand combat. As for the term "stalemate," I have never heard of it before. It appears to have originated with the Tang-Liu battle, as reported below:

From Beijing, the fourth day: After the clash between Liu and Tang in eastern Chahar, the two sides have been in a stalemate for days.

"Stalemate" is indeed a novel term. If this term was coined by a journalist, and it most likely did not come from Sun Wu's military treatises, then the journalist's genius is truly admirable. This is because, with these three words, he not only reported the news but also conveyed the essence and nature of this and countless previous and subsequent wars, exhibiting the style of Sima Qian. I remember seeing the so-called "wheel battle" technique in novels when I was young. This involved several people taking turns fighting one person, exhausting them and making them easier to capture. Its form resembled the rotation of a wheel, both symbolically and figuratively. Those who used this tactic were often dealing with a strong enemy. Although this method had the suspicion of the many bullying the few and lacking heroic spirit, it was justifiable when facing a formidable foe. The meaning of "stalemate" is likely a derivative of "wheel."

However, the merits of the two can be discussed.

The form of a saw is one moving east and one moving west, one going back and forth, one advancing and one retreating, seemingly close yet distant, with the utmost leisurely grace. The two seem to be fighting, but in reality, they complement each other. The only thing suffering is the wood in the middle. In this orderly struggle, sawdust falls, and the parts gradually separate. As for the two sides "sawing," they can always maintain this pattern, pulling back and forth, advancing and retreating, without needing to change or facing any danger. The only thing that changes is the wood. The method of a stalemate is similar. One "aggressively attacks," then the other "retreats"; one "counterattacks," then the other "retreats again." This back-and-forth, advancing and retreating "bombardment" is no different from the form of sawing. "Wheel battles," on the other hand, are different. Although the tactic seems clever, it ultimately has the appearance of being vicious and extreme, which is not favored by refined gentlemen. In the process of the war, there is also the danger of the gears grinding on the skin or getting stuck in the mud. This is likely the reason why modern tacticians abandon the "wheel" and adopt the "stalemate" tactic. This is also an evolution of tactics. Recorded for future historians of culture to reference.

The Path to Renewal Chen Laohuai is Released from Prison 284

— Jing Jia

On the morning he left the prison, he was brought before the warden. The warden said a lot to him, teaching him to be a good person in the future and to run on the path of renewal. He must never commit crimes again. He could only look at his own belly with melancholy.

His body was free, but his stomach was shackled. In prison, he could work and have food to eat; but after his release, where could he find work and food? Looming before him was a dark, cold, and hideous city, its mouth wide open, ready to swallow the insignificant him!

He remembered the warden's words about renewing himself, and he could only force a bitter smile. How could he not know to be a good citizen? He had hands and a brain; he was born the same as everyone else!

Lao Huai had graduated from middle school and had even received several colorful so-called diplomas. But those pieces of paper couldn't be exchanged for food. He had lived an extremely difficult and miserable vagrant life in the city. Because he was a man, and only a middle school graduate, he could never find a job. So he had to commit crimes, using improper means to steal other people's property. Eventually, he was sentenced to six months in prison. He didn't feel much grief about going to prison. At least, in prison, he could avoid the expense of begging for a large pancake, as he had to do outside. It was something that couldn't be helped. When a person is hungry and cold, he has no ability to resist. A good will cannot bind a starving and freezing person.

But now he was released from prison, and the same bitter cold and pain from before would come upon him again.

At first, he thought of begging. Later, he felt that he could never endure the life of begging. He should find some work; he wanted to wash away the shame of his previous crimes with his strength, sweat, and blood.

So he wandered, unconsciously, into a store: "Is there any work for me to do? Anything at all."

As a result, he was kicked out.

The physical pain sobered him up, and he smiled bitterly. This was the suffering he should endure. He didn't have any acquaintances. Could he ask them to give him some work?

He wandered, unable to return to his hometown, unable to find work, unable to even get a sesame cake. Society treated him like a cat treats a mouse. He received no sympathy; he only received cruel jeers.

In the end, he died. He didn't check into a hotel and take sleeping pills, nor did he leave behind a grand and detailed will. He died unnoticed by society in a foul-smelling ditch. He was free from pain, and his soul received its final comfort.

Is death the only path to renewal for him?

Silkworm 285

— Zhong Zhu

"Is there any meaning to life now?" Before the question of whether people have a definite destination after death is resolved, we must first acknowledge that it is meaningful. If people truly have a definite destination after death, then life in this world is nothing more than a fleeting moment. It doesn't matter if you are born and die young because this world is not your permanent abode; you will leave it sooner or later. If people have no soul after death, and there is no permanent place to go, then we should see life in this world as extremely meaningful, and not waste a single moment. We should strive to accomplish something so that we do not waste this life.

But before this question can be resolved, we only have two paths to take. If you see life in this world as meaningless, then you don't need to make "passive attitude," "enjoying the moment," and "reciting Buddhist scriptures to cultivate the next life" your mantras. You might as well commit suicide because living in this world, dragging out an ignoble existence, is no different from living like a parasite. It doesn't benefit you, and it only adds another parasite to society. It doesn't matter if this person exists or not. However, the general public may be using these mantras to blind people's eyes while secretly doing things that harm life. We must not tolerate these parasites. They cannot exist, nor can we allow them to exist.

If you see life in this world as meaningful, then get up immediately. Whether life in this world is meaningful or not, it is like a play on a stage. There are protagonists, supporting characters, and extras in the play. On this stage of the world, no one dictates what role you play. You can be a protagonist, a supporting character, or even an extra, depending on your efforts. Then your life in this world will not be in vain. Otherwise, living aimlessly in this boring era and in this boring country is even more meaningless.

Change 286

— Yu Gui

The sky is so low that it seems to be pressing down on our heads. The weather is so sultry that it's hard to believe it's late autumn after the Double Ninth Festival. The sky over Shanghai, as seen through the window, seems as if the tall buildings are about to fall. In such weather, the most likely to evoke sadness, isn't it? Warm like early spring with a gentle sun, yet without the lightness and vitality of spring, perhaps a more appropriate metaphor would be something like the plum rain season. In this room, staring blankly at the sky, is a sensitive young man with long hair, deep eyes, and a gaunt face. As if feeling some pain, he keeps his brows tightly furrowed as he looks out the window, and from morning until now, we have not seen him shift his gaze.

The room he occupies is a small upstairs room, with just enough space for a desk, bookshelves, and a bed. Everything in the room is piled up in a disorderly fashion, just like the thoughts of the owner of this small building at this moment. On the wall by the window hangs an enlarged half-length portrait of a young woman. She is smiling, as if recalling something pleasing, so innocent, so charming. If the young man's gaze were fixed on this photograph, perhaps we wouldn't be guessing without any reason.

Indeed, he raises his head, looks at the glass of the portrait, tidies his hair that has been blown forward by the wind, and suddenly smiles and walks out.

Outside the door is a bustling street, everything is seething. As the young man steps out, he is surrounded by a group of rickshaw pullers, but he doesn't say a word. He calmly steps over the rickshaw shaft and heads towards the quiet road without looking back. He lowers his head, his hands in his trouser pockets, his leather shoes tapping the cement blocks on the sidewalk. This kind of aimless behavior is a new attitude for him. He has been like this for the past few days.

He walks to a tram station, glances westward, and seems surprised that he is not planning to walk to the French Park, and laughs to himself. Perhaps he has no definite destination. He shows his pass to the Annamite policeman in front of the French Park and steps inside. Suddenly, he seems to be struck by something and stops short. The young woman in the photograph in his room is smiling and greeting him as if she has been waiting for him. Of course, he did not expect to meet her in such a place, but although he immediately returns the greeting calmly, his unnatural attitude is immediately obvious to the young woman.

"Wei, did you receive my letter?" the woman asks.

At this moment, he is holding that letter in his hand. After receiving it yesterday, he summoned his courage several times, but still did not tear it open. Now that he has met the author of the letter, he nods slyly instead of answering. The two of them walk along the path into the park, silently, as if not noticing that someone is walking beside them.

"Wei..." she raises her head, sees his sad face, and swallows the words she wants to say.

"What is it?" He is too humble because he doesn't know what she wrote in the letter. If he had a second to read the letter at this moment, he would be overjoyed. So, hearing her hesitant tone, he feels very sorry for Fei. He disguises this by asking, "Fei, how did you think to come to the French Park?"

"Ever since I sent the photograph to your small building, I have opened up my heart. I was originally a carefree woman, and I thought that love could never subdue me, but we have been apart for half a month, and I have been tormented by depression every day. I can't suffer like this anymore. I spend every afternoon here, but going back brings me even greater sorrow, but I can't think of any other way. I mustered my courage for three nights and wrote you that short letter, hoping that you could come here every day to walk with me. I don't have any other extravagant desires..."

Listening to her sobbing that she can't continue, Wei finally sees that her face is already streaked with tears. The indescribable pain in his own heart also makes him want to cry out loud, but he tries his best to suppress it and sighs, saying,

"Fei, when we met, I never expected that we would reach this point today. I have always wanted to see you, but who can allow us to do this? This forced situation is the same for both of us. To be honest, the letter you sent yesterday is still sealed in my pocket..." As he speaks, he takes the letter out of his pocket.

"Then how did you know that I asked you to meet me in the French Park?"

"Alright, Fei," he doesn't answer her question, but continues, "I want to move, move near you, and combine our spirits and put them to work on something. I can't bear this painful depression anymore either."

They both force a smile, as if their abnormal love has achieved a small result.

Where Should We Young People Go? 287

— Shi Zhong

Now our young people feel that the country is suffering from internal and external troubles, with disasters following one another, and that the situation of various countries in the world rushing to compete with each other is becoming increasingly dire. This economic depression makes it easy for our young people to feel panic in their lives, for their thoughts to become polluted and depressed, for their spirit and time to be wasted meaninglessly, and for their will to waver and be buried, leading to many passive attitudes of not seeking progress and abandoning themselves. What a pity and what a terrible phenomenon! Because we young people are the future masters of the country, and the future maintainers of society. If things continue to decline like this, the country will inevitably be in even worse shape than it is now. This is also true of the world. Although the current miserable state of young people is caused by the poisonous legacy of feudal education, the unequal distribution of wealth and the unreasonable social system, and the foolish selfishness and aggressive magic of the maintainers of world society, we should also deeply investigate these causes. And what songs are popular in various countries now? They are nothing more than what industrial revival, what five-year plans and ten-year plans, what heavy tariffs on foreign goods, what protection of domestic goods and reduction of export taxes, what controls, what emphasis on the martial spirit of self-defense, what new military equipment. We dare not criticize these various declines of various countries, but simply want to expand their own power to compete for markets and plunder other people's property to remedy the lives of their own people, ignoring the overall rise and fall of the world. In short, they are still seeking revival along the old path of foolish selfishness and aggression, and not earnestly improving systems that adapt to the rational life of the times and carrying out industrial revival at the same time. I am afraid that the future results will not be optimistic. Therefore, the hope of a peaceful world is bound to be remote. If we young people harbor the idea of ​​quietly waiting for a time of peace and prosperity to realize our ideals, this is impossible. Or, as a result, we will develop passive thoughts and gradually become polluted, which is even more wrong. We young people should think about who created the world. It was not a god, nor was it a hero or a great man. It was created by the evolution of each individual's thoughts. To put it another way, who created the past economic depression? It was created by each foolish and selfish self in the past. As such, we young people should bear the responsibility of creating a future of balanced happiness and a rational social system. Do not simply blame others, but complain without a sense of responsibility. Simply put, the world cannot be created and maintained by the talents of one or two people. Happiness cannot be enjoyed solely by relying on others. It can only be obtained by the collective activities and struggles of each individual self, all bearing the responsibility of creating and maintaining society. This is what the times are telling us. We young people feel that it is necessary to eliminate all the bad habits and inferior traits inherited from feudal society, cultivate noble thoughts, a courageous spirit, and a firm will to overcome all difficulties, so that we can gradually achieve the goals of our young people's rational aspirations. Here are the attitudes we hope our young people should have now.

1. Do not let panic about life pollute and depress noble thoughts.

2. Do not let panic about life waste a courageous spirit and time meaninglessly.

3. Do not let the fact that people with little learning in society control everything shake and bury the will to study.

4. Do not retreat because of plans for vanity.

5. Do not be passive because it is difficult to find work in society.

6. Do not commit suicide because of the broken rivers and mountains, the difficult national steps, and witnessing tragic scenes.

7. Do not be disgusted with death because of the loss of love.

8. Do not hold on to feudal dreams and wait.

9. Continue to pursue deep-seated thoughts of learning.

10. Revive the spirit of courage, reverence, and diligence in doing things.

11. Have a firm will to seek rational survival in a bright future.

12. Eliminate the bad habits and inferior traits cultivated by feudal dreams and customs.

13. Seek hard work to remedy real life, without shying away from thousands of hardships.

14. In addition to hard work, continue to read books and newspapers for a few hours every three days.

15. Study carefully the causes of past economic depressions in society.

16. Bear the responsibility of creating happiness in your own life and balanced happiness for a rational social existence.

In summary, we sincerely hope that our young people will never shrink back and wait quietly in difficult circumstances, because the evolution of the world never stops. Individual life cannot be delayed temporarily in terms of food, clothing, housing, and transportation by waiting quietly. We only allow our young people to abandon all vanity and seek a way out by working hard and making gradual progress, so that they can have a bright future. In today's society, if you don't have power, there is absolutely no chance to get anything easily, no matter what you do. Therefore, you have to create your own opportunities in difficult times. Whether you should work or farm, work hard and study at the same time. Only by having a firm will, a fighting spirit, and an individual can you achieve a life of happiness, and the country will have a day of true revival.

Life 288

— Sun Wei Lao San Cooperative

We left our hometown one month after we got married. Our union was both old-fashioned and experienced changes within a month of the bride entering the door, forcing us to leave our hometown and throw ourselves into the embrace of Shanghai. Naturally, we had no love to speak of before marriage; after marriage, we had no honeymoon to spend. Fortunately, the law that the beginning of love in old-fashioned marriages comes after marriage did not deceive us. After escaping the oppression of our hometown and living in this small building in Shanghai, no one could believe that we were only a newly married couple of one month. Although Wei is young, she is very knowledgeable and knows the general situation. Because my initial job in Shanghai was as a newspaper reporter, I had many friends and a wide range of social activities. Wei was able to handle the people coming in and out of our small building with grace, even when I was not at home. As for household affairs, she was able to cook and sew, and she loved cleanliness. Although the small building was only three feet wide, it did not make people feel uneasy. As for our income, plain clothes and simple meals were enough to make do. It seemed that we needed a little angel between us, and Wei often looked forward to it.

Our union and daily life were as described above. He could be said to be outside all day, rarely having more than half a day to sit at home. I knew that he was not neglecting his love for his wife; he was living for the lives of both of us. But what does a young woman who has left her mother's arms and become a wife hope for in a lonely foreign land? A little angel, that's what I was hoping for. However, two years were added to my age record after marriage,

Page 22

and my hope was still in vain.

So Wei transferred her love to a kitten. Last autumn, she brought home a white cat, with only two shallow gray spots the size of copper coins on its back. Wei specially made a small quilt for it and laid it in a wooden box. Every night before going to bed, she would coax it into the room in a daze, gently pick it up, put it into the wooden box, and then she would fall asleep peacefully. Later, the kitten also knew the scheduled time. When the time came, there was no need to call it. It would obediently sleep in the wooden box, its head and limbs all curled up, its back slightly undulating, and those two shallow gray circles also rising and falling strangely, which looked very cute. Wei always clapped her hands and said, "This cat is so good!"

Although cats are indeed lovely animals, I love cats because they relieve my loneliness. When I have nothing to do, I hold it and play with it. Its front paws can wash its face, and it can also raise its head and ask people to kiss it. It had gone missing for two days. I searched everywhere, but I couldn't find any trace of it. She said, "I'm afraid we'll have kittens to play with." Sure enough, after it came back, its abdomen gradually expanded. I prepared everything for its birth, and this spring it gave birth to two kittens as cute as its mother. At this time...

At this time, after three examinations by the doctor, Wei was already pregnant, and the ardent desire for a little angel was gradually approaching reality. She forgot about the kitten's birth and made plans for the little angel, buying many cheap fabrics, wool, and even a cradle. Wei prepared everything; and at this time, the white cat disappeared with its two kittens. Did it know that it was going to lose my wife's caress, or did it no longer need human help? Two days before Double Ten Day, our little angel landed with a cry. He left his mother's womb and saw this world. He cried, what was he crying for? No one knew! Although new hope grew from the mother's heart, it could be seen that a pure little soul had entered this turbid world!

— Lie Huo (列火)

(I)

When the seasons cycle to this point, nature presents such a scene: apart from the lingering spring rain and the relatively somber and desolate suburbs, nature is vibrant and lush under the warm spring sunshine, stirring restlessness. The wheat ears in the fields sway in the spring breeze, like the soft fur under a calf, with ripples radiating a myriad of colors. Birds on the branches, welcoming the rich fragrance of flowers, flap their wings to gather the wine of spring, singing songs in subtle harmony. At this time, the men and women in the village no longer appear as withered and listless as they once did, but are all vividly working leisurely in the mountains and fields, clearly a result of the power of spring.

In such springs of the past, my feet would never stay still for a moment; but today is different. The reason is simple: I am now a restless, imaginative student, and, moreover, I am currently being severely punished.

Movie Special

The Daily Lives of Child Actors: They Understand Thrift and Waste Nothing; Mothers Offer Patient Guidance, Never Excessive Indulgence 291

— Mao De (茂德)

After writing a few days ago about a lovely child in Hollywood and how Hollywood film companies protect their major actors, I felt quite interested in the lives of these child actors. Now I will write another article about the daily lives of these young actors and how they spend money, to tell ordinary Chinese children, especially those from wealthy families, to learn their thrift, benevolence, and many other virtues.

Speaking of these many clever and lovely children, ordinary people generally believe that their ability to dedicate themselves to the screen is a lucky and accidental occurrence. Of course, among many clever and lovely children, they alone can dedicate themselves to the screen, while there are still many other clever and lovely children who cannot. This point cannot but be attributed to fate. However, we must know that the status and fame enjoyed by these children dedicated to the screen are truly well-deserved. Among them, there are no stupid, silly, or annoying children. Therefore, this cannot be entirely attributed to fate. They each have their own genius, and once discovered, it can be said that ordinary children are far behind. Sometimes, this kind of genius is indeed something that can only be encountered by chance. Often, a company tests hundreds or thousands of children and cannot find one that is satisfactory, but accidentally encounters one that succeeds as soon as they are in front of the camera.

Although the appearances and actions of these child actors have spread all over the world, and they earn more money than many bankers and wealthy merchants, their parents rarely lack understanding and indulge them, fostering their arrogant and violent temperaments. Among these child stars, the most gentle and refined is David Torrence. One day, a reporter visited his mother and saw him at the door, playing with a homeless kitten. He was teaching it English. The kitten was mouse-colored and very dirty, something that ordinary children would not want, but David asked his mother, "Mother, can we keep this cat? It's so pitiful, it has nowhere to go!" David's salary averages $500 per week, which is equivalent to almost ten thousand Chinese dollars per month, but for each film he makes, his mother only gives him five dollars, and he saves all five dollars. His mother said, "David never knows how to spend money!"

Jackie Cooper is considered to have the highest salary among child stars. His salary is $1,300 per week, which is equivalent to more than twenty thousand Chinese dollars per month, but Jackie himself has never seen the money; his mother collects it all. In the past, his mother gave him fifty cents a week. Now that he is getting older, his allowance has recently been increased to three dollars a week, but he has to buy his own breakfast. Sometimes, the neighboring children can eat some ice cream because Jackie likes to make friends.

There is also Dickie Moore, who, according to his mother, is very wasteful. His mother gives him ten cents a day, but he spends it all as soon as he gets it. He still owes his mother twelve cents, and he probably owes his father fifty cents. When Dickie heard this, he seemed very embarrassed and took twelve cents from his little purse and gave it to his mother, saying, "Mother, I'm not wasteful, I'm returning your twelve cents. I talked to my father about the money I owe him, and we agreed to offset it with hugs and kisses, so I don't have to pay him back." Dickie Moore's weekly salary is $450, but when he has free time, he still wants to sell newspapers to earn some pocket money.

There are also many child actors who enjoyed great fame in the past. For example, Jackie Coogan, who made films for several years and earned a lot of money. Some say he had as much as five million dollars. He is now grown up and has entered university, majoring in drama. There is also David Lee, who co-starred with Al Jolson in "The Little Rascal." He was once a sensation, and theaters across the country invited him to perform on stage, earning a large salary of $4,500 per week. But he has now grown up and can no longer play children's roles. He has also entered school. He is likely to have the opportunity to return to the screen in the future, because film companies often receive requests for him to return to the screen.

Film Reviews

"Mother's Pilgrimage" “Pilgrimage” 丨丨 Grand Theater 丨丨 292

— Mi Wu (蘼蕪)

▲ Introduction

Like Chinese films, American films have recently touched on some social issues. This is certainly a welcome phenomenon, although sometimes objective reality can be distorted by subjective consciousness. But American artists are unwilling to close their eyes and create completely unrealistic stories in their minds, which has already been proven.

▲ "Mother's Pilgrimage"

I honestly recommend this "Mother's Pilgrimage" to Chinese film practitioners and film critics. This is not to say that "Mother's Pilgrimage" is an outstanding film. I recommend this "Mother's Pilgrimage" because it is a very noteworthy film, at least in a few points.

The story simply says, "The son has a lover, but the mother is stubborn and does not want them to be together. She arranges for her son to go to war, where he dies. Later, she sees another couple in the same situation, their affectionate state, and greatly regrets what she did in the past, strongly advising the other couple's mother not to insist on her own views, allowing them to be together, and even welcoming her widowed daughter-in-law and grandson to live with her"!

Of course, this story is not for patriots, because the mother's sending her son to the army is entirely to destroy his love affair. This story is realistic, but it is conceptualized. Because it does not explain the essence of this kind of fact, but only explains the regret of personal emotions, it is not enough. And the reason why I specifically recommend this film to practitioners is first of all because this film is set in the countryside. There are too many Chinese films with a rural background. I hope our practitioners will look at other people's films with a rural background. Secondly, Chinese films, which feel narrow in subject matter, should expand in other directions. A story like "Mother's Pilgrimage" is one way. (Of course, I don't want to completely copy it.)

Now I will write down some of the techniques of screenwriting and directing.

First, the young man returns from the field, panting heavily, and it is obvious that the work is too tiring, so the mother tells him to rest. But as soon as the mother walks away, he is eager to see his lover, running quickly without any tiredness. This is a very real and detailed depiction.

Second, the young man goes to his lover's house at night, and the mother opens the window and looks out because the dog barks. She sees him because the dog and the young man have been close before, so the dog barks as the young man walks away. This is extremely reasonable!

Third, the mother makes him go to war because she does not approve of the young man's actions. Therefore, when the news of the young man's death in battle arrives, her grief is not deep. She only goes to the room and puts the already torn photos back together to look at.

Fourth, when the young man goes to war and gets on the train, his lover sees him off. After the scene of the train leaving, there is a close-up of the lover's face. At this time, he adds the sound of the train. The sound of the train wheels goes from slow to fast, and her facial expression goes from normal to tragic. With a whistle, tears burst out, and the sound of the whistle goes from near to far, and the picture slowly "fades in." The whistle finally cannot be heard, and the picture also fades to nothing. This combination of sound and image is used very appropriately, allowing the audience's visual and auditory senses to feel it at the same time!

Fifth, he uses chickens and dogs as intermissions in the story, which are not just decorations, but are simply related to the plot. The second point above has already explained this.

Sixth, he tightly grasps the mother's personality and develops the story. Before the mother regrets it, he always portrays the mother as an extremely strong woman. Even after the regret, her actions are extremely firm, without much hesitation.

Seventh, the flashback scenes are used appropriately. At the same time, not only is the light in the flashback scenes different from the general scenes, but the flashback scenes also flash by extremely quickly and without stopping, so that people know at a glance that this is a flashback.

Eighth, he writes the mother's regret, which must be at the time of going to France to pay tribute, on the day of seeing a couple in the same situation. This is different from unconditional and immediate realization.

Enough, I have listed eight noteworthy points. Finally, I should also say that the actress's performance is also good.

Review of "Striving for Success" The Man Who Dared 丨Fox Production Nanjing Premiere丨 293

— Ling He (凌鹤)

Generally speaking, a movie story that is stretched out too long often makes people feel scattered and disorganized. "The Turbulent Times" which was recently premiered, also had a lengthy story. From 1800 to the end of the Great War in 1918. However, because of the success of the director, and all the staff were very cautious, the evaluation of that film did not ignore other technical advantages because of the length of the story.

This film "Striving for Success" also has a lengthy story. From the end of the American Civil War in 1871, to three generations of grandparents and grandchildren, extended for more than sixty years. Because so many years of facts have to be performed in a few thousand feet of film, on average, each paragraph can only occupy a small part of the film very simply. Moreover, because the director is not good at handling it, we only see very fragmented details in this film, and we can never find a more detailed description.

We are not saying that long stories are always unacceptable, but that a central point must be grasped and developed as much as possible, and unnecessary parts should only help the development of the central point. Now we may as well study the screenwriting.

In this film, it is very obvious that the author wants to exaggerate the existence of democratic politics as much as possible. Therefore, the playwright explained that the protagonist, John, followed his poor parents to the United States as an immigrant when he was very young. His father died in a mine explosion, and he himself became a miner after growing up. However, because of the encouragement of his parents and his own bravery and perseverance, he finally became the mayor of Chicago from a worker. Finally, he was mistakenly killed by thugs who assassinated the president, replacing the president's disaster. Since the theme is to explain the rationality of so-called democratic politics, there is no need to write about this so-called brave man from sixty years ago. At most, the playwright only needs to explain that John's father was a miner and had great hopes for his son. Then, I think it is enough to start writing about his future aspirations and achievements, starting from the time his father heard the whistle at breakfast and went to work, and died in the mine after encouraging him. At the same time, it is more important to focus on when he achieved his success, and it is not impossible to relax after he achieved it. There are many paragraphs in the middle that can be abandoned, such as marrying a younger sister and giving birth to a daughter. At least these key points can be mentioned in conversations. In particular, the speeches and interviews with reporters in the last few paragraphs are even more dull because the dialogue is too long.

The director used many "fades in" and "fades out", making people feel very fragmented. However, some dissolves are still interesting. The playwright is like this, and the director is also like this, so this ordinary movie is formed.

In addition, the performers do not show anything that makes people excited. The male protagonist plays from youth to old age, and there is no change in age shown in the actions. Especially when he is old, he feels even more like a failure. However, the actors who play John's parents are relatively impressive, although there are not many scenes, they give people a sense of reality.

It is natural for Americans to exaggerate the democratic politics that are popular in the United States in this way. However, whether a worker can really achieve success in this way, I hope we don't have such delusions. However, the author's attempt is ridiculous after all. Especially after the crazy "The West Wing", there are such works appearing, which makes us feel that the American film industry is really strange.

Review of "Ubangi" 丨New Light Screening丨 294

— Moore (摩爾)

The significance of beast movies has been correctly pointed out by many film critics. Of course, it is nothing more than encouraging the public to develop the frontiers and satisfying people's curiosity.

Originally, if beast movies used the method of newsreels, without adding a story, and only introduced the living conditions of wild beasts, it would not be impossible to increase some knowledge for those backward areas and people who do not have zoo facilities. Unfortunately, they insist that every beast movie must lead to a tasteless story.

"Ubangi" is also this kind of movie. Its characteristic is just that it makes its role more complete. It seems like in the middle:

(1) Black people lick the fat from the bones of beasts.

(2) Black people steal and drink the animals' drinking water.

(3) White people whip black people to make them obey orders.

All are trying to depict the black people as foolish, obedient, and deceptive. Not only that, he also wrote that white people give black people Western clothes to wear, and reward them with thunder, to deepen their deception. I remember half a year ago, several beast movies ended with a most loyal and hardworking black man, wearing Western clothes, happily dining with white people in the dining room of a large steamship. The reason is too clear.

The first thing a "beast movie" needs is tension, because wild beasts are indeed very fierce. At the same time, it is not enough to satisfy the curious audience without extreme tension. Therefore, "King Kong" and the like do not hesitate to use photography techniques to increase its tension and horror, but this "Ubangi" is too relaxed. The reason is that the "wild beasts" are not made to act. This is of course the director's responsibility.

In terms of shots, close-ups are used too little, so that the audience does not pay much attention to the "wild beasts". It is also wrong to pay attention to the soft and beautiful scenery as much as possible, without paying attention to the steep mountains. Because this can also make the film relax.

The Literary Film Feast Is Hard to Repeat Dinner at Eight (10) 295

— Ma Teng (馬騰)

Paula's face was pale and her expression absent. She wanted to talk to her mother, but Mrs. Millicent Jordan was too busy to care about her daughter's trivial matters. Her husband said he was also sick, which made her even angrier. She said to her husband, "You're sick? Do you know what I'm like? Today is the first day I've felt better! The servants fought and broke up, the doorman was arrested, and today I have to find a newsroom. The vegetables are ruined again, and today I can only use canned crab meat. What's even more outrageous is that the Flickertons aren't coming! Those two old fossils just called to say they've gone to Florida! You're sick! I'm the one who should be lying in bed! I'm really suffering! Neither of you knows!" After she finished speaking, she walked away in a fit of anger. Oliver and Paula, father and daughter, looked at each other, too scared to say anything, and had to go and change their clothes.

It was long past eight o'clock. The Packards and the Talbots had also arrived. Relatives who were not invited in advance but were brought in to make up the numbers had also arrived. Millicent rallied her spirits and greeted them, not showing any signs of anger. She announced to Packard that the Flickertons were not coming, saying that Lord Flickerton had contracted a sudden illness and had to be sent to Florida immediately. Packard glared at his wife, with indescribable pain in his heart. Millicent took the couple to join the Talbots. Packard and Talbot talked happily about golf and horseback riding. But what about Paula? What about Oliver? What about Larry Renault? What about Carlotta Vance? Could this meal be eaten? When could it be over? She thought listlessly. Finally, she ordered them to have cocktails first.

Oliver came in? His face was green and white. He had just had a sudden attack. Talbot used first aid methods and saved him. Millicent looked at him with infinite tenderness when she saw him. How ashamed she was for scolding him mercilessly just now. Dear Oliver, his illness had already been explained to her by Talbot. How could she leave such a kind, patient, and sweet husband? She decided that after Paula and Ernest were married, she would go to another place to recuperate. Ernest had already arrived, and Millicent greeted him. But what about Paula?

Paula's maid secretly told Mrs. Jordan that Paula was not in her room. Where had she gone? But she had already gone out. A tragic "goodbye" on the phone made her rush to Larry Renault's hotel. When she arrived, countless people were surrounding Larry's door. The door had already been broken down. Suddenly, someone grabbed her hand and pulled her into a room next door. It was Carlotta Vance. Paula cried out madly, "Let go, let go, let me go! Why are you holding me! I want to see him; I can save him!" (To be continued)
